    In One Minute : REST (REpresentational State Transfer)
    REST (REpresentational State Transfer) is an architectural style that uses identification of resources; manipulation of resources through representations; self-descriptive messages, and hypermedia as the engine of application state, to build distributed systems that are scalable and resilient to change. The term was introduced and defined in 2000 by Roy Fielding in his doctoral dissertation. Fielding is one of the principal authors of the Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) specification versions 1.0 and 1.1. In simple language, REST is an alternative to SOAP based web services. Where SOAP tries to model the exchange between client and server as calls to objects, REST tries to be faithful to the web domain. Resources Representational state transfer, on Wikipedia, Architectural Styles and the Design of Network-based Software Architectures, Fielding's dissertation introducing REST, and his clarification regarding the necessary usage of hyper-text in REST APIs implementing-rest on Google Code. implementing-rest with Spring. How to GET a Cup of Coffee RESTful Web Clients Enabling Reuse Through Hypermedia RESTful Web APIs RESTful Web Services Cookbook Solutions for Improving Scalability and Simplicity RESTful Web Services for the real world  ( 6 min )
    What is Turborepo and Why Should You Care?
    Author: Muhammad Khabbab Monorepos are very popular in modern application development because of their immense benefits. A monorepo is a single repository having multiple distinct projects with well-defined associations. Note that monorepo is not a monolith; in fact, it is the opposite of a monolith. It is very easy to make cross-cutting code changes across different applications (/backend, /frontend) in a single atomic commit. It also provides a single source of truth for various environmental concerns you would want to be applied uniformly across your organization. Some examples include dependency management, code reuse from shared packages, etc. Because of the powerful features of monorepo that tech giants like Google and Facebook have adopted monorepo.     Next 13 - Server and Client components
    With Next 13 the team made quite big changes regarding how components render. So let's take a closer look at how rendering works in Next 13. We'll first have to address what is seen as the server and the client. Server: A actual server that hosts your code can receive a request, do some calculations and send back a response once those are complete. Client: The browser a user's device sends a request to the server and does some calculations in the browser to render the correct layout. As you can see, the tipping point lies in where the calculations happen. So what exactly did the ecosystem look like before Next 13? In general, with React, everything happens on the client side.     SocialBoat for Women ‚Äî App for 100M women in India to get fit
    @SocialBoat Today we launch SocialBoat for Women. Motivation to create this came from my mom's (@seema_jain3) fitness journey. I have seen the handwork and struggles she put in to get fit and how it essentially transformed her life. Some critical problems that I saw - 1. Lack of time My mom used to manage the home, and this essentially made her mornings and evenings very busy. Mid day is usually too hot to workout outside and fitness centers are usually closed at this time. I would see her get up at 5am :sunny: everyday, to go for her quick 30 minute walk. 2. Lack of relevant programs My mom gained a lot of weight post her pregnancy, and she struggled to find any relevant programs to lose it. Most gyms had male oriented bulk up programs, and fitness classes were usually too intensive for her. She started learning Yoga from a book, and then Pilates from YouTube videos. She tells me it took her 4 years to gain the confidence she had back in college. 3. Her New Program for women After her at home transformation, she learnt jazz and hip hop dance, performed at multiple venues around the country and recently started a fitness program for women called - Yogalates. An amalgamation of yoga, pilates and dance for women. She takes classes on zoom and more than 100 women have joined her program. Scaling up the concept Our goal with SocialBoat is to take some of these learnings and make high quality fitness accessible to >100M women around the country. - A program one can follow from their home - Is accessible anytime during the day - Tailored to women specific needs - Evolves with different life stages Excited to see how people at ProductHunt find it. Please reach out to us if you have any questions or suggestions! Thank you ‚Äù Discussion | Link  ( 4 min )

    Wishbear ‚Äî Personal wishlists for friends & family
    @tw__ recently got into programming and so we decided to build a small project together. It was important to us that it had a manageable scope but was still useful. So we agreed to build a wishlist app that let's you organize your wishes and share them with your friends and family. There are already dozens of apps like this out there with similar features, but we found them incredibly frustrating and confusing to use, therefore our goal was to try and build an app that works better and has a more modern look. Some highlights of the Wishbear üêª app: - üë§ No registration required, starting to use the app is literally just a single click of a button. Your session will be stored in your browser but you can submit your email address at any time in order to access your wishlists on other devices. - ‚ú® When you add a wish from a link to an online shop, the product details will be loaded for you automatically. That works for almost every shop out there, with a few exceptions that don't provide metadata or block our crawler. - üîê Visitors of your wishlist can mark your wishes as reserved so that nothing is given away twice.     Why sysadmins should choose Awesome window manager on Linux Seth Kenlon Wed, 11/09/2022 - 03:00 Awesome is a window manager for the Linux desktop. A "window manager" is a graphical interface that primarily (if not literally) just manages the drawing and arrangement of windows. In practice, even the most rudimentary of window managers actually provides a little more than just the ability to draw a window. Most also provide a pop-up menu so you can launch an application, some provide a dock or panel so you can switch between different applications you have running.
